### B881 — Bottom map furniture overlaps when a docked panel narrows the map pane (scale bar ↔ "● Scaled" badge ↔ coordinate chip) `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #ui  *(Claude-spotted 2026-07-18 while diagnosing the setback bug — owner's Mueschke Rd screenshot, Parcels panel docked; handoff `handoffheaderandfurnitureglitches.md` NEW-1. Minted **B881** via `npm run next-id -- --against-main`. Code/tests carry the provisional label; a late renumber touches only this heading + V362.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — zoom-/data-density-dependent rendering; the sandbox proves geometry headless, but the live docked-panel eyeball on planyr.io is the class's gate) → V362.** On the in-planner Site map, with the Parcels panel docked (map pane collapsed to ~250–300 px), the graphic scale bar, the "● Scaled" calibration badge, and the lat/long+elevation coordinate chip piled onto each other — "Scaled" overlapped the `500 / 1,000` scale numbers into an unreadable mush.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-18 from the header/furniture handoff (Claude-spotted, NEW-1).
- **Root cause:** the bottom furniture was corner-pinned by fixed offsets in `SitePlanner.jsx` — coordinate chip `left:10 bottom:8`, calibration badge `left:56 bottom:40`, scale bar `right:14 bottom:40`, north arrow `left:14 bottom:40`. B609 verified the chip clears the `bottom:40` band, but nothing accounted for the **badge (`left:56`) and the scale bar (`right:14`) sharing that row**. The badge is the one text-width item (the scale bar auto-caps to the viewport, the north arrow is tiny), so as the pane narrows its right edge runs into the scale bar's left edge.
- **Fix (width-aware, pure + measured):** new pure `calibBadgePlacement` in `sheetFurniture.js` decides — from the true pane width, the measured badge width, and the scale-bar plate dims — whether the badge would collide; when it would, the badge **lifts to its own row just above the scale bar** (clearing the bar below AND the bottom-right zoom controls above, which start at `bottom:100`) and its width is **capped so it truncates with an ellipsis** instead of overflowing. Wide panes keep the original bottom-row layout unchanged. The badge's natural width is measured in a `useLayoutEffect` off the label's `scrollWidth` (cap-independent → no raise↔measure oscillation; pre-paint so no flash — VIEWPORT-STABLE). The coordinate chip also gets a `maxWidth` + ellipsis so it can't run off a narrow pane. The true (unclamped) pane width is now tracked as `size.rawW` (the existing `size.w` is clamped to 320 for the coordinate math).
- **Verified (sandbox):** new unit tests in `test/sheetFurniture.test.js` (+5: `calibBadgePlacement` — wide keeps `bottom:40`, never raises before measure, lifts+clears the zoom row when narrow, and **ZERO badge/scale-bar/zoom overlap across paneW 240→1200 × badge 120–260 × bar 120–240**). Headless harness `ui-audit/bottom-furniture-harness.*` + `bottom-furniture-verify.mjs` drives the REAL furniture plates at 6 pane widths (260→800) and asserts no pairwise bounding-box overlap among scale bar · badge · north arrow · coordinate chip · zoom controls — **91/91 checks, 0 page errors**; screenshots confirm the badge lifts+ellipsizes at ≤320 px and rides the normal row at ≥360 px. Full suite (4260) + lint + build + MAP/backlog-index green.

### B880 — Setback offset line "messes up" on zoom-out: scale its dash + stroke with zoom and drop it when the inset goes sub-pixel `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #ui #selection  *(owner-reported 2026-07-18 from chat — "the lot lines mess up when i zoom out"; clarified as the parcel SETBACK offset ring, `settings.showSetback`. Sandbox-diagnosed handoff (Mueschke Rd / Tomball). Minted **B880** via `npm run next-id`. Branch `claude/planyr-tsakiris-verification-sugso8`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + unit-tested this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — zoom-/data-density-dependent render + PDF/print export-parity classes) → V361.** On a large tract with `showSetback` on, the dashed setback ring read clean at site zoom but on zoom-out crowded/garbled the boundary into a doubled line and (on denser traces) broke into ragged dashes; clean again on zoom-in.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-18 from chat (owner); sandbox-diagnosed handoff.
- **Root cause (verified):** the setback rendered `strokeWidth={1.25}` + `strokeDasharray="7 6"`, both FIXED screen-px — neither scaled by the B617 zoom factor `zk = view.ppf/0.35` (B617 scaled the boundary's WEIGHT; nothing scaled the setback or any dash PERIOD). Two effects: (1) **sub-pixel inset** — a 25 ft setback on a ~2,900 ft tract collapses to ~2 px off the boundary at the reported zoom (<1 px further out), so the dashed ring sits on top of the solid boundary → the garbled double-line (hits even a CLEAN trace, the dominant driver); (2) **fixed-px dash disintegration** — edges shorter than one 13 px "7 6" cycle can't render (6/42 → 42/42 edges as you zoom out). The GEOMETRY was RULED OUT: `offsetPolygon` returned 0 self-intersections across 7→56-vtx tracts / 25→100 ft setbacks (the handoff's withdrawn NEW-2 clipper rework is unnecessary).
- **Fix:** new pure `lib/lineZoom.js` — `dashZoom(spec, zk)` (mirrors `strokeZoom`: scales the dash period by `zk`, floors it so the period never goes sub-pixel `DASH_ZOOM_FLOOR_PX=3`, caps at 3.5×) + `insetRingVisible(minInsetFt, ppf)` (a dashed inset ring draws only when its smallest inset reads ≥ `INSET_MIN_VISIBLE_PX=3` on-screen px; below that it's SUPPRESSED, reappearing on zoom-in). The setback ring now suppresses when sub-pixel, runs its weight through `strokeZoom` and its dash through `dashZoom`. **PDF-PARITY:** `printSheet` clones the live SVG, so the scaled dash/weight carry to export by construction (B617/B719 precedent — no separate export path).
- **Sibling dashes folded (handoff item 4):** the utility/deed/easement spines + neutral markups (via the shared `da` source) + the overlay-calibration connectors now fold through `dashZoom` too — the same latent B617-sibling class. Transient draft/cursor overlays deliberately stay fixed-px.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** dash-scaling sibling of **B617** (weight only) and **B719** (to-scale curb). Net-new; no prior item scales a dash period.
- **Verified (sandbox):** `test/lineZoom.test.js` (10: dashZoom no-op at zk=1 / floored on zoom-out / capped on zoom-in / solid + unparseable passthrough / multi-segment; insetRingVisible visible/suppressed/threshold/non-finite) + `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` new B880 guard (setback uses insetRingVisible + strokeZoom + dashZoom, not fixed 1.25/"7 6"; the `da` source folds through dashZoom). Full suite green + lint + build green + MAP regenerated.
- **⏳ V361 (live/headless, planyr.io):** see VERIFICATION.md — draw a large parcel, setback on, zoom fully out → a clean continuous dashed inset that cleanly DISAPPEARS once indistinguishable from the boundary, never a garbled double-line; PDF/print export matches.

### B871 — Berm materialization: an applied TOB raise becomes modeled dirt with full downstream propagation `[Site Planner]` (feature) #site-planner #yield #pond #floodplain #grading  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-16 as "NEW-6"; minted **B871** via `npm run next-id -- --against-main`. Branch `claude/detention-verdict-delta-bugs-l3mm1l`.)*
`[ ]` **IMPLEMENTED this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — real-project-data (Tsakiris 144–159′ reach) + apply→heat-map/ledger/label round-trip + undo) → V354.** A TOB above grade was a number with no dirt behind it.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-16 from chat.
- **Per-cell materialization:** new `pondGeom.bermFillCells(ring, det, { gradeAt, wseFt, ratio, triggerClassAt, fpId })` — crest at TOB, outer face at the pond side slopes, height = TOB − LOCAL grade PER-CELL off the 3DEP grid (tall on the low side, absent on the high side). Returns cells + heatCells + volCf + floodCf + toe ring + landTakeSf + maxHeight + crest. Below-WSE, in-trigger cells are the compensating-fill contribution.
- **Propagation** (SitePlanner `pondBerms` rewritten to consume it, per-cell when a grade sampler exists, else the median constant):
  - (a) **mitigation ledger** — the below-WSE berm prism joins the fill set and raises the requirement (`pondBermFloodCf`, already folded via `addCf`); intersect acreage bumps so a berm-only intersect never mis-reads "no fill"; the existing berm-as-fill fixed-point feeds NEW-5's preview.
  - (b) **fill-depth heat map** — the below-WSE berm cells join `fmResultView.cells` (engine-truth: Σ cells × ratio == the ledger contribution, unit-tested).
  - (c) **land take** — the fill-berm toe ring joins the maintenance-berm ring in the pond inspector's true land take (the greater reach governs); collision checks extend to it.
  - (d) **earthwork** — berm fill CY (`pondBermFillCf`) joins the ledger, netted against basin cut, with "berm can be built from basin spoil — haul math is your engineer's".
  - (e) **pond inspector/label** — berm height + crest elevation shown; the banded diagram's TOB line moves with the applied TOB.
  - (f) **rules copy** — in-trigger berms keep the berm-as-fill warning + the Waller note (1:1 offset · §A(9)) + the conveyance caution (a ring levee can block flow — engineer's check).
- **Edge cases:** TOB at/below grade → no berm (dormant, never a zero-height ring polluting ledgers); partial in-trigger berms price only in-trigger cells; the NEW-5 TOB remedy on an unanchored pond is gated (the assistant refuses without an anchor).
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** extends B833 (the berm-as-fill mitigation contribution) with per-cell height + heat-map cells + land take; not a recurrence.
- **Verified (sandbox):** `pondGeom.bands.test.js` (+6: cells+volume+toe+land-take; dormant at/below grade; heat-cell tie-out Σ==floodCf; no-trigger → earthwork-only; per-cell height varies; degenerate → null). Full suite (4196) + lint 0 errors + build green.
- **⏳ V354 (live):** see VERIFICATION.md.

`[ ]` **IMPLEMENTED + sandbox-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — concurrency/multi-writer, a mandatory-live class) → V334.** Repro (owner, ×2: 2026-07-14 truck-court depth; 2026-07-15 Bain `smr9olizi5ue` building edit ~15:55Z): two signed-in tabs of one account on one plan, second tab idle; a cascade edit in the active tab → burst of B673 remote-upsert toasts for the DERIVED elements the gesture re-laid (paving area, sidewalks, parking fields — never the element actually touched), each "you (another window) changed a … you just edited — their version is showing"; bonded aprons can visibly separate for a beat; refresh clears it.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-15 from chat (owner-reported 2026-07-14 + 2026-07-15).
- **Root cause (per the handoff diagnosis, confirmed in code):** (1) `processResults` stamped `recent` for EVERY ok result with no user-touched vs derived distinction, so cascade outputs answered `authoredRecently` — any foreign-looking echo of them toasted "you just edited"; (2) since B674 the second tab is a live writer, and the pending-edit journal was ONE KEY PER SITE (`planyr:elements:pending:<siteId>`), so an idle tab's refetch could fold-and-clear the active tab's mid-commit journal — re-committing its in-flight edits as byte-divergent copies that passed every single-tab self-echo guard (`SitePlanner.jsx` conceded the clobber in a comment); (3) `reconcileSeedRows` could substitute MIXED shadow pairings (a newer adopted rev over an older kept json) into a refetch re-seed — the "aprons separate for a beat" churn.
- **Fix (all three handoff directions shipped):** **#1** `createElementSync` takes `isDirectEdit(kind,id,el)`; every enqueued op carries a `direct` tag (preserved through conflict/missing/exists re-enqueues; `restore()` always direct) and **only direct ops stamp `recent`** — SitePlanner supplies "bonded (`attachedTo`) elements are derived unless the gesture/selection (drag/sel/multi, stamped every render into `directTouchRef`) targeted them". **#2** new exported `semanticallyEqual(a,b,eps=1e-6)` (numbers within eps, key sets must match — gates only WHO IS TOLD, never what is written): a semantically-equal live row is now SILENT on all three read paths (conflict branch → adopt rev with our bytes, no re-commit ping-pong, no event; pending branch → no `remote-while-dirty`; no-pending upsert → no `remote-upsert`). **#3** the journal is **per-SESSION** (`planyr:elements:pending:<site>:s:<tab>`, sessionStorage-backed id): a live sibling's journal is untouchable, orphans (frozen `at` > 5 min) + the legacy key are adopted-and-swept, same-tab reload recovery unchanged; plus shadow entries whose json was KEPT under a newer adopted rev are flagged `stale` and `reconcileSeedRows` never substitutes them (fetched row stays canonical; the post-seed reconcile re-commits any newer local truth).
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** net-new — the TWO-tab path. B757/B759/B811/B812 are the SINGLE-tab family (implemented, parked V273/V301/V303/V304) — not reopened; their guards are regression-tested unchanged. B673/B674 built the toast matrix + multi-writer cutover this hardens.
- **Verified (sandbox):** 16 new unit tests — `test/elementSync.test.js` (derived ops never claim authorship + direct guard + tag survives re-enqueue + restore/fail-open/default-direct; semantic-equality unit cases + all three silent paths + genuine-difference guards; stale-pairing seed hardening + clean-entry B759 behavior preserved), `test/elementJournal.test.js` rewritten (per-session isolation, live-sibling hands-off, orphan adoption + sweep, legacy migration, own-beats-orphan dedupe, reload recovery, session-id stability), `test/elementRows.test.js` (stale guard), `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` (SitePlanner wiring source guards). Full suite + lint 0 errors + build green; e2e smoke/canvas specs green. Element sync runs signed-in only — the sandbox can't sign in, hence the live park.
- **Adversarial review (4-lens find→refute workflow) — confirmed findings all fixed same session:** (1) `sweepJournals` unconditionally deleted a FRESH legacy journal `readJournal` had refused to fold (a live pre-upgrade tab's crash protection destroyed) → sweep now consumes exactly the read's key set; (2) read/sweep used two `Date.now()` calls, so a journal crossing the 5-min orphan boundary in between could be swept unfolded → one shared timestamp; (3) the autosave effect reconciles BEFORE the render-effect stamp, so a single-shot edit after >10s idle enqueued against aged stamps (a directly-edited bonded child mis-tagged derived) → `stampDirectTargets()` also runs at the top of `reconcileElems`, same tick as the enqueue; (4) skipKeys-filtered journal entries were discarded with zero telemetry → now reported via `onDiscard` (LOUD-FAILURE). **Accepted, documented limitations:** browsers copy sessionStorage on "Duplicate tab", so a duplicated pair shares one journal id — for that pair only, behavior falls back to the pre-fix shared journal (strictly no worse; a liveness protocol isn't worth the boot cost, and foldJournal's baseRev guards cap the blast radius); with sessionStorage BLOCKED (but localStorage working) the per-load fallback id makes a reload's own journal look foreign for the 5-min orphan window — recovery is delayed, never lost; panel-driven edits to bonded children (e.g. "+ add zone" with the building selected) tag derived — quiet-side-only cost (a softened heads-up, never data).
- **⏳ V334 (live, planyr.io, SIGNED IN, two tabs):** see VERIFICATION.md.

### B839 — Export aerial reuses cached basemap tiles instead of a slow on-demand render (fixes the timeout that blanked the PDF) `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #export #gis #perf #stitching  *(follow-on to B738/V252; owner-dropped 2026-07-15 as the aerial-export "NEW-1" — distinct from the same-day panel-flash NEW-1 → B837, and from the 2026-07-09 NEW-2/NEW-3 folded into B738; minted **B839** via `npm run next-id`. Branch `claude/aerial-export-imagery-cache-vr03je`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + headless-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — PDF/export parity + zoom-/DPI-dependent tile rendering + GIS-endpoint behavior, all mandatory-live classes) → V329.** With the Esri "Aerial" basemap on, a normal/large frame → Download PDF printed on white with "⚠ Couldn't load the satellite imagery…" though the map looked fine on screen. The export now sources the aerial from the SAME fast, pre-rendered tiles the live map shows, so the slow dynamic render is no longer the failure mode.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-15 from chat (owner live console test, project `smr9olizi5ue` — Katy, 5 parcels ~110 ac).
- **Root cause (live-confirmed from the planyr.io console):** `exportAerialForFrame` requested a **fresh on-demand dynamic image** (`aerialPlacement` → `BASEMAPS[basemapSrc].export`, `maxPx:2400`); Esri's `World_Imagery/MapServer/export` renders that frame in **>8 s**, and `inlineImages`/`fetchAsDataUrl` abort every fetch at the shared `INLINE_TIMEOUT_MS=8000` → the `data-export-aerial` `<image>` is dropped → `aerialDropped` → `flashWarn` (owner console: Esri `export` **AbortError @ 8015 ms**; USGS `export` **200, 1255 KB, 4022 ms** for the same frame).
- **Fix (fast path):** `exportAerialForFrame` is now async and STITCHES the covering XYZ tiles (the browser/CDN-cached tiles the live Leaflet basemap already displays) into a frame-exact data: URL, instead of a dynamic `/export`. New pure Web-Mercator math in `lib/arcgis.js` — `lngLatToGlobalPixel` / `aerialTileGrid` (covering tiles + cropped-canvas size + per-tile draw offset) / `pickAerialTileZoom` (deepest zoom ≤ the source's `maxNative` that keeps the canvas ≤ maxPx — never past the ceiling, or Esri/USGS return the gray "no data" placeholder as HTTP 200, the B182/B220 trap). DOM stitch (`fetchTileImage` + `stitchAerialDataUrl` in `SitePlanner.jsx`) crops to the exact bbox and returns a JPEG data URL, **reusing `aerialPlacement`'s feet geometry unchanged** (Mercator↔linear differs sub-pixel over one site; we anchor to the same bbox corners). The live tile layers now request **`crossOrigin: true`** so those bytes are canvas-readable and the stitch reuses the same cache.
- **Fallback chain (LOUD-FAILURE preserved):** stitch active source → stitch alternate source → dynamic `/export` placement (rescued by B840's longer budget + alt-source retry) → only then dropped + a loud warning. STRICT stitch (any missing tile → fall back) so an exhibit is never gappy. A stitched data: URL is skipped by `inlineImages` (no fetch), so the common case has no timeout at all.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** net-new — no item reuses cached basemap tiles for the export backdrop. Builds on **B738** (the export-aerial machinery) and **B202** (the time-boxed `inlineImages` + `dropOnFail`). Cache prior art (reuse, not dupe): **B445** (server-side Drive imagery cache), **B438** (browser SW+IndexedDB, superseded by B445), **B694** (cached vector tier). Distinct from **B171** (gated evaluation of a higher-res imagery *source*).
- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** new pure tile-math tests in `test/aerialExport.test.js` (Web-Mercator pixel origin/scale, bbox crop dims, full tile coverage with in-range indices, zoom clamps to `maxNative` + stays under maxPx) · **B839 source guard** in `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` (stitch + crossOrigin×2 + async + both callers await) · **new `ui-audit/verify-aerial-tile-stitch.mjs`** drives the REAL stitch DOM path in headless Chromium against a local CORS tile server: all-tiles → a **941×941 JPEG data URL, 100% non-white, canvas NOT tainted**; one 500 tile → stitch returns **null** (strict-fails to the fallback). Existing `ui-audit/verify-aerial-export-cors.mjs` still green. Full suite + lint 0 + build green; MAP.md regenerated (new `arcgis.js` exports). NOTE: the live Esri/USGS tile fetch can't be driven from the *sandbox* browser (the egress proxy resets headless Chromium's TLS to arcgisonline / blocks nationalmap) — same limit as V252; a real browser at planyr.io has no proxy.
- **⏳ V329 (live, planyr.io — no sign-in):** on the owner's Katy site (or any large multi-parcel site) with the **Aerial** backdrop ON, **Download PDF** → the satellite is the background (not white), aligned under the parcels/massing, and it comes back **promptly** (no ~8s stall, no "couldn't load" warning). ### B840 — Interim: aerial-specific inline timeout + retry + Esri↔USGS source fallback on export `[Site Planner]` (task) #site-planner #export #gis  *(follow-on to B738/V252; owner-dropped 2026-07-15 as the aerial-export "NEW-2"; the hardening layer beneath B839's tile stitch; minted **B840** via `npm run next-id`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — timing/timeout + GIS-endpoint fallback + PDF/export parity) → V330.** The safety net for when B839's tile stitch can't run (a source's tiles unreachable): the aerial no longer shares the small fetches' 8 s cap and no longer drops on the first slow render.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-15 from chat (owner live console test).
- **Change:** `fetchAsDataUrl(url, { timeout, retries })` takes a per-call budget + retries; `inlineImages` gives the `data-export-aerial` image its own **`AERIAL_INLINE_TIMEOUT_MS = 22000`** budget + **one retry**, and — like an overlay — retries its **`data-fallback-href`** on failure. For the aerial that fallback is the **alternate source** (`exportAerialForFrame` attaches the Esri↔USGS `/export` URL for the same bbox), so a slow primary (Esri `/export` timed out where USGS answered in ~4 s) is rescued silently before the aerial is dropped. The small tile/overlay fetches keep the 8 s cap (unchanged) so no export gets slower.
- **Build on, don't reinvent:** extends **B202**'s existing `inlineImages` time-box (no parallel path); the source switch reuses **B693**'s `BASEMAPS[basemapSrc]` registry.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** net-new — no item owned an aerial-export-specific timeout/retry/source-fallback (`INLINE_TIMEOUT` lives only in `SitePlanner.jsx`). Relatives: B738 (machinery), B202 (the time-box), B693 (the source selector), B839 (the fast path this backstops).
- **Verified (sandbox):** **B840 source guard** in `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` (`AERIAL_INLINE_TIMEOUT_MS`, the `isOverlay || isAerial` fallback branch, the new `fetchAsDataUrl` signature). The timeout/retry/alt-source rescue is a timing + live-endpoint behavior → confirmed live in V330. Full suite + lint + build green.

### B837 — Left-rail panel switch flashes the basemap and jumps the site sideways `[Site Planner / Map + UI]` (bug) #site-planner #ui #perf  *(filed from chat 2026-07-15; minted **B837** via next-id — renumbered from a provisional B835 on merge, which collided with PR #623's Scheduler B835; DEDUPE-FIRST: distinct trigger + new symptom vs B821 — see note)*
`[ ]` Desktop, project open: clicking a left-rail icon to open/switch the left panel (reported on **Parcel**) makes the aerial **flash** (tiles wipe + reload for one frame) AND the drawing/parcels **jump horizontally** a large distance (~a couple hundred feet at working zoom; in the reported case the massing landed on the neighborhood to the west, well off its true parcels). Expected: opening/switching a left panel is seamless — no basemap flash, drawing/parcels stay locked to the aerial in their real-world position (zero sideways shift).
- **IMPLEMENTED 2026-07-15 (parked ⏳ Verify → V328).** **JUMP fixed:** the `panelShiftRef` compensation now measures the ACTUAL canvas left-edge (`wrapRef.offsetLeft`, relative to the position:relative body row) in a `useLayoutEffect` — same-paint, before-paint — instead of an assumed `leftWidth + 6` in a passive (after-paint) effect. Reconciling the measured delta cancels EXACTLY for any panel width, a live rail-resize, AND a panel→panel switch, with no one-frame skip; a phone overlay (position:absolute, B556) and a floating card (portaled out, B717) contribute nothing to `offsetLeft`, so it stays desktop/docked-only with no conditional. **FLASH fixed:** the formerly-separate un-ghosted `map.invalidateSize(false)` (fired ~60ms after the ghosted commit on every `size` change — the residual tile-wipe) is folded INTO the `sizeChanged` branch: `spawnGhost()` → `invalidateSize` → `setView` now run under ONE B65 ghost, and `size` was dropped from the standalone invalidateSize effect (now `active`/show-hide + origin only). Added a viewport-transform seam (`data-view-offx/offy/ppf` on the canvas SVG) + e2e `e2e/panel-toggle-viewport.spec.js`. **AUDIT-FIRST correction:** the assumed `leftWidth + 6` actually equals the real stolen width for the default same-width case, so the SETTLED position was already correct — the user-visible defect is the multi-frame skip on a heavy project (passive effect lands several frames late) + the un-ghosted aerial wipe; the layout-effect + folded ghost close both by construction. Headless-verified LOGGED OUT (seeded 1-parcel site, real origin): a fixed feet point holds its viewport x to **0px** across open / switch→Analysis / switch→Yield / close, zero console errors; build + full suite (`e2e/panel-toggle-viewport.spec.js` green) + lint green.
- Verify: live (timing/state + zoom-/data-density-dependent rendering — LIVE-VERIFY. **Measure before patch (mandatory):** instrument on live planyr.io via Cowork, reproduce rail→Parcel from BOTH panel-closed and panel-already-open-on-another-tab, and confirm the mechanism before writing any fix.)
- Origin: filed 2026-07-15 from chat (owner-reported).
- **Two symptoms, two subsystems (hypothesis — confirm by measuring first):**
  - **Jump** = the SVG-canvas pan-compensation effect (`panelShiftRef` in `SitePlanner.jsx`). It shifts the canvas to cancel the width the docked panel steals, but models only ONE rail width (the persisted resizable-rail width) and reconciles only on `leftPanel` truthiness. If the Parcel panel renders at a different width, or a panel→panel switch changes the canvas width without the compensation trigger changing, it over/under-shoots and the drawing slides by the mismatch.
  - **Flash** = the Leaflet resize path. The seamless zoom/pan system (transform-zoom + ghost-buffer) treats a container resize as "no prior view worth ghosting" and does an immediate hard `setView` → Leaflet `_resetAll` removes and reloads every tile for a frame. The panel toggle hits this un-buffered branch.
- **Measure before patch (mandatory — timing/state class):** capture map-container width before/after, each panel's actual rendered width, `panelShiftRef.current`, `view.offX` before/after, and whether a Leaflet resize/`setView`/tile reload fires. Confirm whether the jump is (a) width-mismatch in the compensation, (b) a one-frame ordering gap between the pan-shift commit and the flex reflow, or (c) panel→panel width change with no compensation — before touching code.
- **Fix direction (once confirmed):** compensate against the *measured* canvas-width delta (drive off a `ResizeObserver` on the map container, not an assumed `leftWidth + 6`) so any panel width and any panel→panel switch cancels exactly · apply the pan-shift in a layout-effect keyed on the observed size so it lands in the same paint as the reflow (no one-frame skip) · ghost-buffer the resize commit (a panel-toggle resize DOES have a valid prior view — spawn the ghost like zoom-out already does, hold current tiles across the `setView`, drop them on the tile-layer `load`). Reuse the existing mechanism; no new dependency. Do NOT hard-code an offset for one panel's width — it masks the stale-size root and drifts on other panels/screens/rail resizes.
- **Files likely touched:** `src/workspaces/site-planner/SitePlanner.jsx` (the `panelShiftRef` effect + the geo commit / ghost resize path). No projection/coordinate files.
- **Gotchas:** keep B556 intact (phone panel overlays are position:absolute, resize nothing → compensation stays desktop/docked-only); B717's floating panels don't resize the canvas either, so exclude floaters from compensation; verify the switch doesn't re-trigger Web-Worker overlay parsing (would re-render overlays and read as a second flash).
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** minted fresh + cross-linked (NOT a re-open), following B821's own precedent of minting fresh against B65 for "a distinct trigger reaching the same subsystem through the branch a prior fix left un-buffered."
  - **B821** (⏳ Verify → V310, shipped) — same *flash mechanism* (docked-panel resize → un-ghosted `setView` tile-wipe) but a different trigger (single/double-click feature-select) and it does NOT cover the horizontal jump. ⚠ If the flash still reproduces live after B821 deploys, B821's V310 live-verify is implicated — check B821 first when measuring.

### B864 — Scheduler meeting-body lost to a multi-writer clobber: bound tasks kept an ORPHANED meetingBodyId (election date at risk on reload) `[Scheduler / persistence]` (bug) #scheduler #persistence #infra  *(discovered 2026-07-16 during the B863 hs-v1 sweep; minted **B864** via `npm run next-id -- --against-main`)*
`[ ]` **DATA REPAIRED (V345) + (a) orphaned-binding hardening (V346) + (b) the root-cause multi-writer MERGE (V347) all IMPLEMENTED + sandbox-verified 2026-07-16 across three PRs; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — concurrency / multi-writer, a mandatory-live class). (b)/V347 CONFIRMED PASS live 2026-07-19 (two-tab same-cell conflict test) → VERIFICATION-DONE. V345 + V346 live click-throughs still remain (both blocked on a real signed-in hs-v1 session — see VERIFICATION.md).**
- Verify: live
- Origin: discovered while filing B863 (protocol: a diagnosis reaching the repo mints a B# on sight).
- **What happened (live hs-v1):** two Goose Creek tasks — #86 "Organization Meeting" and #88 "Conduct Confirmation Election" — were `meetingBound:true` pointing at `meetingBodyId: mb_mrmdy43mlhjr`, and #88 carried a correctly-computed election date (2027-05-01) + agenda deadline (2027-02-12) — yet `settings.meetingBodies` was **null**. The calendar definition was never persisted while its BINDINGS were: an orphaned reference. Owner's words fit a stale-tab clobber ("maybe I went over to a tab that didn't update"): the app cloud-saves the WHOLE document last-write-wins, so a second tab lacking the just-created body saved over the tab that had it.
- **Why it bites:** on a fresh load, `cascadeDates` sees `meetingBound:true` but no body in `bodyMap` → `bound=false` → the task falls back to a plain FS date (loses the election date), and **B836's drift guard would then "heal" #88 away from 2027-05-01** to that wrong FS date (a loud rewrite of an intended date).
- **Repair (this session, safe window):** reconstructed the correct **Texas Uniform Election Dates** calendar under the same id `mb_mrmdy43mlhjr` (recurrence: 1st Saturday of May + the Tue-after-1st-Monday November uniform date; agendaLead 78cd to reproduce the 02/12 deadline), **engine-verified it reproduces #88 = 2027-05-01 / deadline 2027-02-12 exactly** and leaves #86 blank + 83/85/87 unchanged, then persisted it via a guarded surgical `jsonb_set` (guard: only write if `meetingBodies` isn't already an array — cannot clobber a concurrent re-save). Re-query confirmed 1 body present, #88 unchanged, post-repair drift = 0.
- **(a) CODE HARDENING — IMPLEMENTED + sandbox-verified 2026-07-16 (own PR, per the meeting-binding/`cascadeDates` own-PR rule):** `cascadeDates` now computes `bodyMissing` (a `meetingBound` leaf whose `meetingBodyId` isn't in the body index) and, when the task HAS a stored date, **soft-pins it** (`t.pinnedStart || (bodyMissing && t.start)`) so preds can't overwrite the intended meeting date + sets `t.meetingBodyMissing`; a bound task with NO stored date still falls through to normal FS scheduling (unchanged). `detectCascadeDrift` now **exempts** `meetingBound` + `deadlineForTaskId` rows (their dates are calendar-/anchor-derived, not simple-cascade drift — like pins), so a legitimate re-snap (or a preserved orphan) never fires the drift banner. The row surfaces the formerly-INVISIBLE broken binding as a danger-toned calendar + alert dot with a plain-English tooltip ("Bound to a meeting calendar that no longer exists… re-create/re-select in Settings → Meeting Calendars, or unbind"). Mirrored in `ui-audit/stress/scheduler-engine.mjs`. **8 new unit tests** (`test/schedulerEngine.test.js`): missing-body preserves the date + flags it; unbinding the same task DOES revert to FS (proves preservation is real); present-body snaps + clears the flag; drift-exemption for meeting + deadline rows; source guards on both files + the badge. Full suite (4176) + lint 0 errors + build green. **→ V346** (the row badge is signed-in-board-only — the embed can't boot headless, B644/B501).
- **(b) ROOT CAUSE — IMPLEMENTED + sandbox-verified 2026-07-16 (own PR):** the whole-document cloud-save was last-write-wins with a rev-gate that only BLOCKED a stale tab (snapshotting the loser to history + forcing a reload that dropped its edits) — so a sibling's just-created calendar was lost when the other tab won. **AUDIT-FIRST correction to B850's "Scheduler is two-tab-safe" claim:** the guard blocks the *loser*, but the loser's changes never reach the cloud, and the write itself (`sb.upsert`) is an unconditional whole-doc overwrite — no field-level merge. **Fix:** on a would-be-blocked auto-save the storage layer now **3-way MERGES** our edits onto the newer cloud (`mergeCloudDoc(base, ours, theirs)`, module scope + mirrored/unit-tested in `scheduler-engine.mjs`) instead of blocking: base = the doc this tab last loaded/saved (`baseByKey`), ours = current, theirs = the newer cloud. A side unchanged vs base yields to the changed side; id-keyed arrays (tasks / meetingBodies / contacts) merge per element by id (adds survive, a delete is honored only if the other side left the key alone); a genuine same-leaf conflict prefers ours, the loser kept as a `premerge-ours` Version-History snapshot. The App adopts the merge via a `planar:merged` event, **reconciling against its CURRENT state** (`mergeCloudDoc(ancestor, current, merged)`) so an edit made during the save round-trip is never lost, + a "Merged in changes from another tab" toast. Falls back to the old block-and-snapshot only when no base ancestor exists (seed/offline). **14 merge unit tests** (the exact election-calendar repro: a stale tab's save preserves the sibling's calendar + binding + its own edit; keyed-array add/delete/conflict; nested project add; missing-base fail-safe) + a full node simulation of the two-tab flow incl. an in-flight edit. Full suite (4188) + lint 0 + build green; `index.html` babel blocks esbuild-parse-clean; `MAP.md` regenerated. **→ V347** (the live two-tab race is a mandatory concurrency LIVE-VERIFY class — can't drive two signed-in boards headless). Residual (smaller, noted): a true simultaneous read-check-write TOCTOU (both tabs at the same rev racing the unconditional upsert) is not closed by this — an optimistic conditional write is the follow-up; the merge handles every non-simultaneous ordering.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** distinct from **B846** (Site-Planner element-sync false-conflict toasts, its own transport) and **B850** (which asserted Scheduler two-tab safety — this is the counter-example); same multi-writer THEME, different subsystem (Scheduler whole-doc save + meeting bodies). Relatives: **B836** (the guard that would mis-heal the orphaned task — now taught to exempt it), **B815/B816** (the meeting-body engine).
- **⏳ V345 (data repair) + V346 (the (a) badge) — still pending, live, planyr.io, SIGNED IN:** see VERIFICATION.md. **V347 (the (b) two-tab auto-merge) — ✅ CONFIRMED PASS 2026-07-19, moved to VERIFICATION-DONE.md.**

Kept in ⏳ Verify (V326).

The silent heal is the real defect: a wrong stored start (B835) was corrected without anyone knowing it had ever been wrong. So the fix makes the existing heal LOUD rather than adding a new recompute.

### B835 — Edit-time cascade gate skipped typed-duration & pin edits: a task's own end updated but successors kept stale dates (×2) `[Scheduler]` (bug) #scheduler #persistence  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-15 as "NEW-1"→**B835**; RE-OPENED as a recurrence 2026-07-16 (chat "NEW-1") — a live hs-v1 repro proved the 07-15 "self-healed, no code bug" close WRONG. Root cause found + fixed: the `updateTask` cascade gate. Per DEDUPE-FIRST this fix carries **B835**, not a new number.)*
`[ ]` **RECURRENCE (×2) — IMPLEMENTED + sandbox-verified 2026-07-16; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — timing/race + real-project-data, not driveable headless: the embed's CDN React/Babel is egress-blocked, B644/B501) → V344.**
- **Live repro (owner, hs-v1 Goose Creek MUD/District Creation):** task 82 "Remove Tract from City of Baytown ETJ" pinned start, `45cd`, end 02/28; its FS successor 83 "Petition TCEQ for District Creation" (no padlock) displayed a stale start; the whole FS chain 83→85→87→88 was frozen. Owner: "the edit committed but successors never recomputed on-screen — stale display + stale persist." Confirmed against live Supabase (`planar_data.hs-v1`): task 83 stored a start its predecessor chain can't produce.
- **AUDIT-FIRST — root cause (the 07-15 close missed it):** every scheduling edit funnels through `updateTask` (`public/sequence/index.html`), whose cascade gate was a hand-maintained OR-list: `if ('duration' in updates || 'start' in updates || …)`. It **omitted `durValue`/`durUnit`** — but the B615 typed-duration path (the grid duration cell `:8374`, the master-view cell `:11217`) commits `{durValue,durUnit}`, **never `{duration}`** — and **`pinnedStart`/`pinnedEnd`** (unpin `:9426`, unlock-finish `:9427` commit `{pinnedStart:false}` / `{pinnedEnd:false,durValue,durUnit}`). So a typed duration edit (or an unpin/unlock) resolved the EDITED task's own end (`durEdited` branch runs) but **never called `cascadeDates`** → successors kept stale dates AND the stale array was persisted. Exactly the hs-v1 repro: 82's duration changed 45cd→45d, its FS successor 83 never re-flowed. The 07-15 audit's claim "`updateTask` recomputes on every date/dependency edit" was true for `{start}`/`{duration}` but false for the `{durValue,durUnit}` + pin-toggle paths.
- **Fix:** replaced the fragile OR-list with a complete predicate — `SCHEDULE_INPUT_KEYS` + `touchesSchedule(updates)` (module scope in `index.html`, mirrored + exported in `ui-audit/stress/scheduler-engine.mjs`); the gate is now `if (touchesSchedule(updates))`. Covers `start,end,duration,durValue,durUnit,predecessors,pinnedStart,pinnedEnd,meetingBound,meetingBodyId,pinnedMeetingDate,minMeetingsAfter,deadlineForTaskId`. Non-scheduling edits (name/health/%-complete/notes/color/focused/isExpanded/responsibleParty/cost) still correctly skip the cascade. **Audit of every other mutation path** (Gantt = display-only, 0 `updateTask` calls; range-fill/master cells route through `updateTask`; delete/indent/outdent/paste/reorder use `recomputeAfterStructureChange` which already cascades; add/insert create blank tasks) confirmed the `updateTask` gate is the single point of failure — this one fix covers "EVERY scheduling-input mutation (start, finish, duration, lag, predecessor set, unpin — typed, pasted, or dragged)."
- **Secondary check (owner-requested):** a calendar-day task ending on a weekend hands off cleanly — `constrainedStartFrom` FS `addBD(Sun 02/28,1)=Mon 03/01` (no skew); unit-locked.
- **Verified (sandbox):** new tests in `test/schedulerEngine.test.js` — `touchesSchedule` fires for each scheduling key incl. the missed ones + the exact commit shapes, and is false for every non-scheduling edit; a fossil-chain test proves 83→85→87→88 re-flow to their predecessor-derived starts once the gate fires; a weekend-cd hand-off test; source guards that both files use `touchesSchedule` + carry `durValue/durUnit/pinnedStart/pinnedEnd`. Full suite (4128) + lint 0 errors + build green; `MAP.md` regenerated (new export).
- **⏳ V344 (live, planyr.io, SIGNED IN):** see VERIFICATION.md — edit a task's duration (type `45cd`), start, lag, or unpin it and confirm its successors re-flow ON-SCREEN immediately (no reload) and the new dates persist.
- **Superseded (07-15 prior pass, kept for provenance):** concluded "no current code bug; the Grand Port task-81 8/03→7/13 fossil predated the cascade-on-edit + load-recascade; the pin was a red herring (forward-only cascade proven via `planar_history`)." That reasoning about the *pin* and *forward-only cascade* stands; the "no code bug" verdict does not — the durValue/durUnit + pin-toggle gate gap is real and is what this recurrence fixes. B501 (delete-path recompute) + B836 (loud load-time drift heal) remain the siblings.
- **⚠ Owner decision (product, still open, logged in `OWNER-TODO.md`):** the old Grand Port 80→81 gap — if a ~15-working-day gap between AHJ approval and civil revisions was intended, encode `lag:15`; else 07/13 is correct. No code blocked on it.

### B832 — Drainage facts auto-revalidate; the ↻ button becomes an override, not a gate `[Site Planner / yield · GIS]` (feature) #site-planner #yield #gis #persistence #perf  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-14 as "NEW-12"; minted **B832**)*
`[ ]` Owner: "do I need to hit check every time? I'd like it to auto update as I move stuff around." The ledgers already recompute live per edit off cached facts — what's manual is the FACTS fetch (zones, WSE rasters, 3DEP, authority), and stale facts silently gate everything downstream.
- Verify: live (timing/debounce + GIS endpoint class — drag a pond within the envelope → instant numbers, no fetch; drag 500 ft outside → one coalesced auto-fetch ~2 s later; offline edit still works with honest stale labeling).
- Origin: filed 2026-07-14 from chat ("NEW-12").
- **(a) Auto-run on load** when there's no in-session check and the remembered snapshot is stale or geometry-incomplete (the B804/B829-class states).
- **(b) Auto-extend on edit:** debounced (~2–3 s after the last edit), re-fetch ONLY when an element's bbox exits the previously fetched envelope or a new fill/pond appears outside it — pure element moves inside the envelope never refetch.
- **(c) Sampled-point facts** (WSE at the fill centroid, grade tile) revalidate when their anchor moves > ~100 ft.
- **(d) Rate-limit + concurrency-cap** per the B366 discipline — a burst of drags coalesces to one revalidation; degraded sources fall to the honest last-good/unavailable states (B367 SWR), never block editing.
- **(e)** ↻ stays as "force refresh now"; the status line reads "facts as of <time> · auto" vs "· manual".
- **(f) Multi-writer care** (2026-07-14 cascade handoff): revalidation writes `lastCheck` idempotently and must not fight a second open tab (the B793 family).
- Cross-links (DEDUPE-FIRST, not dups): B750 (the remembered check + ↻ it upgrades), B804/B829 (the stale/slim honesty states that define "needs revalidation"), B367/B96 (the SWR cache it rides), B366 (rate-limit discipline).
- **IMPLEMENTED 2026-07-14 (parked ⏳ Verify → V324).** `lib/factRevalidation.js` (new, pure): load-kind triggers (no snapshot / stale sig / geometry-incomplete B804/B829-class records) vs edit-kind (the raw feet envelope exits the persisted fetch envelope; the fill-centroid or ground-line anchor drifts >100 ft), with stable per-target keys so a failed attempt never retry-loops; **pure moves inside the envelope never fetch** (unit-asserted, incl. under a stale sig). `checkDrainage({auto})` persists `lastCheck.fetch = {env, anchorPt, groundPt, mode}`; a DEGRADED auto run (authority unavailable, or flood failed where the snapshot had loaded) shows its honest live state but **never overwrites the good remembered snapshot** (last-good; a manual ↻ keeps replace-always). The auto effect: 1.2 s load / 2.5 s edit debounce via effect re-arm (drag coalescing), a ≥20 s rate floor, one attempt per key, skipped while the tab is hidden (multi-writer care — lastCheck writes stay sig-keyed + JSON-guarded). Status line reads "Facts as of <time> · auto|manual" (same-day time); ↻ is the explicit override; `settings.drainage.autoFacts === false` opts out (headless legacy seeds). 12 unit tests (`test/factRevalidation.test.js`); headless case G (a stale snapshot fires ONE honest failed auto attempt in the sandbox, editing never blocked, the good snapshot survives — asserted via localStorage). Full suite + build green.

### B808 — Mitigation volumes integrate per-cell 3DEP grade (retire the single centroid-line median) `[Site Planner / yield · floodplain]` (feature) #site-planner #yield #floodplain #gis  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-13 as "NEW-2"; minted **B808**)*
`[ ]` `computeMitigation`'s depth callback is a zero-arg closure over ONE grade — `depthAt = () => Math.max(0, Math.min(wse, pad) - grade)` (`lib/floodplainMitigation.js:493`) — even though `gridIntersect` already invokes it WITH each cell's point (`:137`). And today's "grade" is weaker than a site median: the median of a 9-sample 3DEP line (~230 ft) through the LARGEST parcel's centroid (`sampleGround`, `SitePlanner.jsx:6175-6181` → `drainCtxData.groundElevFt`). On sites with relief (Bain's corridor falls toward the creek) that single number materially mis-prices fill.
- Verify: live (GIS endpoint + data-density class; note V243's existing-grade expectation needs updating once gradeBasis=grid ships).
- Origin: filed 2026-07-13 from chat ("NEW-2"); upgrades a designed-in limitation of the B707 engine (its spec deliberately chose manual override > the drainage ctx's 3DEP median), surfaced via B712.
- **DEM grid:** fetch a site-extent bare-earth grid via the B704 plumbing — the pure pieces are ready and worker-safe (`lib/demGrid.js`: `gridRequest` / `decodeGrid` (LERC → survey-ft NAVD88 with validity mask) / `maskedSmooth` / `sampleAtLatLng`; `terrainWorker.js`), but the fetch orchestration (`fetchGridBytes`/`computeTile`) is module-private to `terrainLayers.js` and map-tile-keyed — a small site-extent fetch helper is NEW work (compose gridRequest+fetch+decodeGrid, or export/refactor). One grid, cached; site-feet → mercator transform helper.
- **Depth:** `depthAt(pt) = max(0, min(wse, padAt(fp)) − demAt(pt))`; void cells excluded + counted — LOUD-FAILURE if >5% of intersect cells are void.
- **AO design point:** the AO path derives WSE as `grade + z.aoDepthFt` (`floodplainMitigation.js:449`) — decide whether AO WSE goes per-cell too (`demAt(pt) + depth`) or stays median; settle it in the close-out.
- **Fallback:** the median stays as the explicit fallback when the grid is unavailable — result carries `gradeBasis: "grid" | "median"` (extend the existing `elev.sources` provenance idiom, `sources.existGrade 'manual'|'3dep'` at `SitePlanner.jsx:6413`) and the ledger labels the median case ("flat-grade estimate"). Manual `existGradeFt` entry still overrides everything (flat-grade mode, labeled) — that path already works (`SitePlanner.jsx:6400`), keep it.
- **Delta flag:** surface when grid-based volume differs from median-based by >15% — those are the sites where the old number was silently wrong.
- **Retention (feeds B809):** per-cell results retained per footprint×zone — today `gridIntersect` returns only `{ areaSf, sumDepthArea }` and discards the cells (cap `maxCells` 1500 / `minCellFt` 2, `floodplainMitigation.js:118-119`) — same array, no recompute.
- **Unit tests:** synthetic tilted-plane DEM where the closed-form volume is known; void-cell exclusion; fallback labeling.
- **Acceptance (live):** a sloped test fixture prices ≠ median-mode and matches closed form within tolerance.
- **IMPLEMENTED 2026-07-14 (parked ⏳ Verify → V316).** `fetchSiteGrid` (terrainLayers.js — gridRequest + the proxy-first fetch + one main-thread decodeGrid, LRU by req.key, ~≤3 m ground cells) rides the drainage check with failure isolation; `computeMitigation` prices per cell via `elev.gradeAt` (manual grade wins → flat mode; grid → `gradeBasis:"grid"`, provider `3dep-grid`; else the labeled median "flat-grade estimate"); AO zones price the published depth riding the ground per cell, capped by the pad (the close-out decision); voids excluded + counted with the >5% `grid-voids` LOUD flag; the flat-median comparison accumulates in the same loop → the >15% `grid-median-delta` flag with both figures; memo sig carries the grid key (the B807 stale-memo class). 12 unit tests incl. the tilted-plane closed form (±1%). Live: real 3DEP grid fetch + Bain sloped-corridor pricing ≠ median (V316; the sandbox 404s the DEM host).

### B821 — Map flashes/blanks on single- & double-click: docked-panel resize → un-ghosted `setView` tile-wipe `[Site Planner / Map]` (bug) #site-planner #ui #perf  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-14 as "NEW-1" — "the map flashes/flickers every time I single- or double-click a feature/parcel/overlay, then repaints"; minted **B821** (late-bound against fresh main). Implemented + shipped same session; parked for the live click-through. → V310.)*
`[x]` **FIXED this session — root-caused in code, fixed by extending B65's existing anti-flash ghost-buffer to the resize path.** The Site Planner's aerial is a non-interactive Leaflet backdrop under the SVG canvas. Clicking a feature opens a docked side panel that is an **in-flow flex sibling of the canvas** (`SitePlanner.jsx:12119`/`:12141`), so opening it shrinks `wrapRef`; the `ResizeObserver` (`:2486`) calls `setSize`, which re-runs the basemap view-sync effect (`:1682`, deps `[view, size, origin]`) down its `sizeChanged` branch (`:1730`). That branch called `commit(center, z, false)` — **the ghost buffer was skipped** — so a raw `map.setView` fired Leaflet's `viewreset`, whose GridLayer handler **wipes & reloads every aerial tile** = the one-frame flash. It fired on parcel single-click (Parcel panel), element/markup/callout double-click (Properties companion), overlay select (References panel), and click-empty-to-deselect (panel closes) — hence "frequent." (The report's other four hypotheses were each ruled out in code: the map is created once and never re-keyed/remounted on selection; `doubleClickZoom:false` on the backdrop; no per-select layer remove/re-add or `setData` source reload.)
- **The fix (one flag).** `SitePlanner.jsx:1730` now passes `commit(center, z, !!prev)`: first paint (`prev===null`, no tiles on screen to clone) stays un-ghosted exactly as before; a **resize with a prior view on screen** ghost-buffers, so B65's frozen-tile snapshot (`spawnGhost` `:1696`) sits on top until the fresh tiles report `load` and the `setView` wipe never shows. Untouched: the pan/zoom gesture path (`size` doesn't change during a gesture) and initial load.
- Verify: live → **V310** — a single-frame tile-wipe flash is a zoom-/data-density-dependent render the headless sandbox can't capture (the B65 class; the geo aerial also needs a real site + tiles the sandbox egress-blocks), so the live click-through parks for a browser check on planyr.io.
- Origin: filed 2026-07-14 from chat (owner NEW-1).
- **Named rules:** AUDIT-FIRST (traced the real ResizeObserver→`size`→un-ghosted-`setView` chain against B65's ghost machinery, confirming B65 fixed only the gesture path and left the resize branch un-buffered by design); LIVE-VERIFY (one-frame flash → V310); MODULE-SCOPE-COMPONENTS n/a. No `MAP.md` change (inline effect edit — no file add/remove/rename, no primary-export change).
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** net-new number, NOT a B65 recurrence. **B65** ("White flashing on zoom/pan and general redraw", Done) built this exact ghost-buffer, but its triggers were zoom/pan/load gestures and it never regressed for that scope; this is a distinct trigger (click-select → docked-panel resize) reaching the same subsystem through the branch B65 left un-buffered — so a new B# cross-linked to B65, not a re-open. Relatives (not dups): **B741** (angled-element selection handles, live-gated) and **B750** (single-click select vs double-click open Properties) — adjacent selection-interaction items, different symptom.
- **Verified (sandbox, 2026-07-14):** `npm run build` green (SitePlannerApp/DocReview still separate lazy chunks); full suite **3796** tests green (incl. `backlogIndex`/`mapDrift`/`docPointers`/`contrast` guards); `eslint` 0 errors on the changed file (only pre-existing warnings on other effects); headless smoke (logged-out `vite preview`) — entered the planner via "Start blank", single-clicked + double-clicked the canvas → app stays mounted, zero JS/page errors (only an expected egress-blocked tile fetch). The flash itself is not headless-observable → V310.

### B691 — Fort Bend 1-ft contours layer dead: browser CORS-blocks `arcgisweb.fortbendcountytx.gov` — route it through the server-side GIS proxy (×2) `[Site Planner / GIS]` (bug) #site-planner #gis  *(surfaced 2026-07-07 in the Cowork element-sync live run — console showed the layer's `…/FLOODZONE/Contours_1Foot/MapServer?f=json` probe failing CORS on planyr.io)*

Same class as other locked-down county endpoints: route the request through the existing same-origin server-side GIS proxy pattern (a Pages Function fetches server-side, where CORS doesn't apply, and relays JSON to the app) instead of calling the county host directly from the page. Scope: this layer's probe + tile/feature requests; keep the honest per-layer status + self-heal re-probe semantics.

The noise is real UX harm even where the layer self-heals via the proxy retry — silence the DIRECT probe, don't just document around it. (Arrived as chat item "NEW-2"; DEDUPE-FIRST — it is the probe half of this item's existing scope, so no new number.)
- **Scope amendment (2026-07-14, folds in "NEW-2"):** add a `noCors: true` flag on the source/registry entry (`fb_contours`, `counties.js:211-220`) that makes `probeService` (`layers.js:462`) skip the doomed direct `?f=json` attempt and go straight to the B445 GIS cache proxy probe (`proxyServiceUrl`, `src/shared/gis/gisProxyCore.js:50`) — the direct attempt is what prints the red burst (`fetchWithRetry` retries thrown fetches ×3, `layers.js:417-429`, before the proxy retry at `layers.js:470-472`). Constraint carried over from B469's deliberate direct-FIRST design: if the proxy is unreachable/404 (e.g. dev without the deployed Function), fall back to today's optimistic layer add — a `noCors` host's health must not hard-depend on the proxy being deployed. The layer row's ⓘ notes "health via proxy (host sends no CORS headers)". - DEDUPE-FIRST (corrected 2026-07-14 — AUDIT-FIRST: this line originally claimed "no existing B# covers Fort Bend contours or a CORS-proxy route for it", which was wrong): **B469 (Done)** already shipped the `probeService` direct-first / proxy-on-CORS-failure retry for this exact host — this item REFINES that shipped design (the remaining console noise is B469's deliberate direct-FIRST attempt) and extends the proxy route to the tile/feature requests. ### B817 — Float-to-deadline, cost-of-miss, and the cadence view `[Scheduler]` (feature) #scheduler #entitlements #gantt #export  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-13 as "NEW-3"; minted **B817**. → V307. The math is half the product; the decision value is knowing **what one day of slip actually costs**. In an entitlement schedule a day is routinely a month, and nothing in the current grid says so.
- Verify: live — column math + health rollup unit-testable; the Gantt ticks/flags + the two banner resolutions are **V307**, run via Cowork on live planyr.io.

(AUDIT-FIRST: `depElbow`/`depElbowD` in the brief were removed with the elbow router; the current path is `depAnchors`+`glyphEdges`.)
- **Deadline badge** on the driving predecessor's bar ("file by 8/18/26") — the upstream task that actually has to hit the date carries the warning, not just the hearing.

### B816 — Meeting-bound tasks: snap to cadence, auto-roll on miss, derived agenda deadline `[Scheduler]` (feature) #scheduler #entitlements #gantt #perf #export  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-13 as "NEW-2"; minted **B816**. → V306. Implemented + shipped same session; the engine is unit-tested in the sandbox (15 tests), the UI is parked for the live click-through.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — engine + data layer + civic mark + bind picker + roll toast.** Depends on B815. **Own PR, nothing else in it** — this touches `cascadeDates`, the highest-blast-radius function in the codebase (B584/B585/B501/B487/B568 all cluster here). A task bound to a meeting body snaps to the body's cadence, derives its agenda deadline, and **auto-rolls a whole cycle** when the deadline is missed.
- Verify: live — engine end-to-end unit-testable via the verbatim mirror + anti-drift guards; the live click-through (bind a task → slip a predecessor → watch it jump a cycle → pin it → watch it go red) is **V306**, run via Cowork on live planyr.io (the scheduler's CDN React/Babel is egress-blocked in the sandbox).
- Origin: filed 2026-07-13 from chat ("NEW-2").
- **Task fields `_v7 → _v8`** via a new `normalizeToV8` (idempotent), chained after the existing `normalizeToV7` (`:4562`): `meetingBodyId · meetingBound:true · pinnedMeetingDate?`. Existing tasks untouched — a no-op stamp, zero date shift by construction. Run the real before/after diff against the live scheduler dataset (Supabase hs-v1, ~667 tasks) exactly as B621 did. (AUDIT-FIRST: today's version is `_v7`, not `_v8` — B816 adds V8.)
- **★ The agenda deadline is NOT a task row.** It is a **derived field** — a pure function of (body, chosenMeetingDate), recomputed every cascade, never persisted as authoritative, never given an id, never entering `tasks[]` or the dependency graph. Rationale from this repo's history: `renumberTasks`/cut-paste/delete/indent-outdent have each corrupted the task array (B568/B584/B501/B487), so a system-owned row inside a user-owned list reopens all of it; and a real FS link deadline→meeting closes a cycle against the meeting→deadline derivation (`validatePredEdit` rejects it). Precedent: **B583** formula columns (`e:false`, derived, no feedback loop) — except computed *inside* the cascade, because unlike a formula column it participates in date selection.
- **Cascade rule** (in `cascadeDates` `:1861`, after the normal predecessor-derived early start, before `calcEnd`): predecessors produce a packet-ready date; chosen meeting = earliest `m` where **`agendaDeadline(m) >= packetReady`** — NOT `m >= packetReady` (the core of the feature and the obvious wrong implementation; `m >= packetReady` silently puts items on agendas they can't be filed for). `start = end = m`; duration forced to 0d; agenda deadline computed + stored as a derived field for renderers.
- **Tie-break — `sameDayFilingAllowed`, default false:** when the driving predecessor is itself a meeting (first reading → second reading), eligibility is **`agendaDeadline(m) > drivingMeetingDate`, strictly**. Council meets Tuesday evening; the next agenda closed at noon that same Tuesday — a `>=` produces a schedule that cannot physically happen (at a 10-business-day lead on a 2-week cadence the two readings can never be consecutive and the schedule quietly loses a month). `minMeetingsAfter:{taskId,n}` for two-reading ordinances / "must be a subsequent meeting."
- **★ The mark (ships in THIS item — B816 can't land without it).** A bound row breaks three rules other rows follow (date can't be freely typed · duration forced to 0 · slips in cycles not days) — a row that behaves differently with no visible reason is a silent-behavior defect. **Glyph:** a bank/civic mark (`ti-building-bank` from the loaded `ti` webfont, or a hand-rolled SVG to match) in the Start-cell glyph slot beside the padlock (`:8895–8924`), distinct from the amber padlock (`pinnedStart`/`pinnedEnd`, **B621/B622** — in-code labels `B615`/`B616`): padlock = a person fixed this date; civic mark = a meeting calendar fixes it. They co-occur on a pinned bound task (🏛 8/11/26 🔒) — exactly the state that goes infeasible. **Three states, salience tracking severity:** `--text-secondary` (healthy float) · `--text-warning` (≤2 working days float) · `--text-danger` (infeasible — pinned + agenda closed); solid fills; the row tints `--bg-danger` **only** in the infeasible state. **Clicking the glyph explains the row** — body name, cadence, agenda rule, `verifiedOn` stamp, the plain-English reason the date is what it is, and the resolutions (roll to next meeting / unpin / change body). No DevTools, no dialog.
- **Every roll is announced** — reuse **B624**'s toast verbatim: "First reading moved to 8/25/26 — the 8/11 agenda closed 8/4." A bound date that moves without the user seeing why is a defect, not a convenience.
- **Interaction matrix — each case its own test in `test/schedulerEngine.test.js`.** `cascadeDates` already branches on no-predecessors / pinnedStart / pinnedEnd / dep type (FS-SS-FF-SF via the `switch` inside `constrainedStartFrom` `:1740` — AUDIT-FIRST: `DEP_DIRS` was removed with the elbow router, so hook the new case there, not a named map) / lags / unit-aware duration (`resolveDuration`) / blank-unscheduled. "Meeting-bound" is a fifth orthogonal branch, and this matrix is where the bugs will come from:
  - **bound + pinnedStart** → pin wins, do not roll → infeasible flag + red glyph.
  - **bound + pinnedEnd** → nonsense (start==end==meeting date) — reject on entry.
  - **bound + blank/unscheduled predecessor** → stays blank (B386's first-class unscheduled state) — must NOT snap to next Tuesday from today.
  - **bound + SS/FF/SF link** → packet-ready = the normal early start (via `constrainedStartFrom`); snap from there.
  - **bound as a summary/parent** → disallow (parents come from `rollupParentDates`) — guard in `validatePredEdit`.
  - **bound + typed duration** → force 0d with a visible inline error, never a silent zero.
- **Also touches:** `updateTask` (`:5157`) · `previewProject` (`:3728`, must mirror `updateTask` exactly — B585-S1 was a preview that lied about a pinned task) · `mkt` (`:2071`, new-task factory defaults) · `applyUpdate` (`:7875`, typing a date into a bound task snaps to the nearest eligible meeting + toast, mirroring B624's weekend roll-forward) · `validatePredEdit` (`:1705`).
- **Perf (interacts with B256, Open — the live board is already at 667, past its ~500 threshold):** precompute each body's meeting dates once per cascade run (`meetingDatesInRange(body, projectStart, projectEnd+horizon)`) and binary-search — do NOT generate recurrence dates inside the per-task loop. Strongly consider landing B256's id→index + parent→children[] maps first (makes this cheaper, overdue on its own merits).
- **Both Gantt renderers, or neither.** `GanttView.depLines` (screen, `:9296`) and `buildGanttSVG` (PDF/Print, `:10866`) are separate implementations that have drifted (B386/B395/B584 #11) — either put the glyph + markers in both, or have the export render bound milestones as plain milestones — **state which in the PR** (PDF-PARITY).
- **Shipped:** `cascadeDates(tasks, bodies)` + `applyMeetingBinding` (the snap rule `agendaDeadline(m) >= packetReady`, the strict two-reading tie-break, `minMeetingsAfter`), mirrored VERBATIM into `scheduler-engine.mjs` with **15 unit tests + 3 anti-drift guards** covering the whole matrix (bound+pinnedStart→infeasible, bound+blank pred→blank, bound+SS/FF/SF, bound-as-parent disallowed, typed-duration→0, the ★ two-readings-lose-a-month case). Bodies reach the cascade via a global `MEETING_BODY_INDEX` (like `HOLIDAY_SET`; ids are globally unique so no cross-project bleed; `duplicateProject` RE-IDs copied bodies). `normalizeToV8` is a no-op version stamp that refreshes the index on load. UI: the hand-rolled civic-bank glyph in the Start cell (3 severity states + a plain-English hover explainer), a hidden **Meeting** grid column with a native-select bind picker (`updateTask` re-cascades on the meeting fields; `previewProject` mirrors it), and the B624-voice roll toast when a bound task's meeting moves. Full suite green, `npm run build` green, `MAP.md` regenerated, `eslint` 0 errors, scheduler JSX validated via esbuild.
- **Deferred to follow-ups (noted, not silent):** the explainer is a rich **hover** tooltip (a click-open popover is a small NEW-3-era polish); the `--bg-danger` full-row tint is not yet wired (the red glyph carries the infeasible state); direct-typing a date into a bound row currently pins via the normal path (the snap-to-nearest-meeting-on-type is a refinement). **Both Gantts:** bound tasks are duration-0 **milestones**, so they already render as diamonds in BOTH `GanttView` and `buildGanttSVG` (the export shows the plain milestone — the stated PDF-PARITY fallback; the civic glyph lives in the grid). The live before/after diff against the real ~667-task board + the click-through are **V306**.

### B807 — Fort Bend Zone A finally prices: FBCDD Atlas-14 100-yr WSE raster provider (`derivedWse1pctFt`, DRAFT-labeled) `[Site Planner / GIS · yield]` (feature) #site-planner #gis #yield #floodplain  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-13 as "NEW-1", same-day follow-on to the B803–B806 ship; minted **B807**. → V302. ### B792 — Review delete-safety: same-name re-upload cross-wires two reviews; delete permanently destroys the markup layer; a network blip renders an empty Library `[Doc Review / Library]` (bug) #doc-review #library #persistence #drive #files  *(found by the 2026-07-12 data-deletion-safety audit as "NEW-F1/F3/F5/F7"; lineage: NEW-4/B579/B757 delete honesty, B54 read-failure discipline. Branch `claude/data-deletion-safety-audit-bw5xg9`; → V292. RENUMBERED twice on merge-ins of `origin/main` (concurrent sessions took B783, then B784–B790/V285–V290); the code/commits keep the provisional NEW-F# labels.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED — four legs, one path:** **(F1)** `buildDriveKey` embeds `srcId` in the key's LAST segment (`project-<pid>/<discipline>/<srcId>__<name>`) so two uploads of the same-named file can never share a key (the old name-only key REBOUND the `drive_files` mapping to the newest Drive file — the older review's backdrop silently swapped, and deleting either review deleted the one mapped file under the other). Legacy keys resolve unchanged (stored on the source record; the server's flat-folder derivation drops the last segment, so folders are byte-identical). Purge-path byte deletes are gated by a **shared-key guard** (jsonb containment over other rows; fail-safe: unconfirmed → keep bytes + notice). **(F3)** `deleteReview` = SOFT delete (`deleted_at`, migration `doc_reviews_soft_delete.sql` — **applied to production via MCP this session**); Library gains **Recently deleted** (Restore / two-click Delete-forever), worded confirms, a ~10s undo toast; `ReviewsBar`'s `window.confirm` removed (owner rule); lazy 30-day purge; pre-migration DBs degrade to the old hard delete. B757 `.select("id")` + B579 ordering preserved; boot-resume can't reopen a deleted review (`loadReview` hides deleted rows; the local draft clears on soft delete — the cloud row keeps full data for restore). **(F5)** `fetchReviews`/`fetchFileFacts`/`fetchProjects` return `{ok, rows}` (the pinStore pattern); FileBrowser keeps the prior list on a failed refresh + a loud Retry notice — never a fake-empty Library (the panic that walks a user into F1's re-upload). **(F7)** purge also removes the `file_facts` row (full TOMBSTONE-DELETES cascade set). **Post-review hardening (same session — 5-lens adversarial review, 25 raw findings triaged, the real ones fixed):** the `fetchReviews` fallback tiers are now GATED on a genuinely-missing `deleted_at` column (a transient error on a migrated DB is an honest `ok:false`, never a filterless re-query that would resurface Recently-deleted rows); `listDeletedReviews` returns null on a failed read (the bin keeps its last list, mirrors NEW-F5); the automated 30-day purge surfaces stranded-bytes cleanup failures; the undo toast fires only on a delete that really landed (0-row no-op → loud notice, B757 honesty); the bin view can't strand you without an exit toggle; ReviewsBar's row keyboard handler no longer hijacks Enter from the inline confirm, and an armed confirm disarms on menu close. **Accepted semantics (documented in the migration file):** on a TEAM-shared review, any member can bin/restore (rides the member-wide UPDATE policy — same editors who can already rewrite content; recoverable by design), while permanent purge keeps the stricter owner/team-admin DELETE policy.
- Verify: live (real-project-data + Drive + signed-in-only surfaces) → **V292**.
- Sandbox: new `test/reviewDeleteSafety.test.js` (21 cases); headless smoke (planner + Library + Review signed-out states, zero page errors, no native dialogs); full suite + build green.

### B789 — Per-source `timeoutMs` override in the GIS screening-fetch registry (FEMA flood answered at ~9.5 s, past the 9 s default) `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature) #site-planner #gis #floodplain  *(coworker live-diagnosis handoff 2026-07-12 as "NEW-2"; late-bound to **B789 / V289** via `npm run next-id -- --against-main`. Origin: filed 2026-07-12 from chat. Same branch as B790. Implemented + sandbox-verified same session.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED — a GIS source row can now set its own `timeoutMs` to override the shared 9 s screening-fetch default (`GIS_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS`); `GIS_SOURCES.flood` sets 20 s.** During the 2026-07-11 slowdown FEMA's NFHL answered the flood `/query` in ~9.5 s, so all three retry attempts aborted ~0.5 s too early and the Site Analysis floodplain row went unavailable even though FEMA would have answered. The override lets flood wait ~20 s (flood data changes slowly, so a longer wait is cheap) while every other source keeps the 9 s default.
- **Plumbing:** `reg()` (`siteAnalysis.js`) carries `s.timeoutMs` onto the endpoint; `queryLayer`/`countLayer` forward `{ timeoutMs }` into `fetchArcgisJson`, which already honored `opts.timeoutMs ?? GIS_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS` — zero change to the fetch core.
- **AUDIT-FIRST correction to the handoff:** the handoff said the *vector* engine rides "the same 9 s substrate." It does not — `vectorLayers.js` `defaultFetchJson` is a **bare `fetch` with NO timeout**, so the 9 s near-miss is the **screening path only**. The vector flood pull isn't aborted at 9 s (it has its own long TTL cache); this override targets the path that actually lost the race.
- **Caveat (live evidence, do not oversell):** FEMA's own gateway still dropped some responses at ~10 s during the worst of it, so 20 s only rescues the *marginal-slow* case — the durable fix is the SWR cache proxy (**B788**), not this alone.
- Verify: live (GIS-endpoint timing class — confirming the flood screening survives a genuinely slow (~9–10 s) FEMA answer needs the live degraded endpoint; the sandbox can't reach `hazards.fema.gov`) → **V289**.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** a direct follow-on to **B366** (Done — the shared resilient fetch + the 9 s cap it introduced); B366 added no per-source override. Distinct from **B367**/**B371** (the screening cache tiers).
- Sandbox: 2 new `test/siteAnalysis.test.js` cases (flood forwards `timeoutMs: 20000` to the fetch layer; a source without it passes no override → the default applies) + `test/gisSources.test.js` still green (the field is additive, unguarded). Full suite green · lint 0 · build green.

### B782 — Wire the FBCDD Atlas-14 WSE rasters into `derivedWse02Ft` `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature) #site-planner #gis #yield #floodplain  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-12 as "NEW-2" — the B770/V279 wiring follow-up, endpoint locked by the PR #594 cowork discovery. ### B409 (×2) — Unlimited-size file uploads: chunked Drive upload through the Worker proxy (replaces the CORS-dead browser-direct path) `[Doc Review / storage]` (bug) #doc-review #drive  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-23 as "NEW-1"; minted **B409**. REWORKED 2026-07-11 per the owner’s unlimited-uploads handoff, branch `claude/unlimited-file-uploads-04zkc9`; → V282 (minted V280, renumbered on merge-in of `origin/main` — the concurrent jurisdiction-badge/ISD session took V280/V281).)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED (rework) — any-size uploads as ~16 MB chunks relayed through new `/api/uploads/*`; the streaming/Range download half fixes "won't open"; parked here for the live 125 MB round-trip → V282.**
- Recurrence: 2026-07-11 (×2) — the owner's 125 MB "GPL - Civil IFP 2026.06.19.pdf" still can't save. The first fix (browser PUTs bytes DIRECTLY to Google) is **CORS-dead by design and could never pass its live gate**: Fetch-over-CORS hides the `Location` header of the session-init response, and Google's upload endpoint answers preflights with no `Access-Control-Allow-Origin`. Re-opens the ORIGINAL B# (DEDUPE-FIRST) — do not re-attempt browser-direct-to-Drive.
- **Rework (all same-origin, so CORS never applies; owner decision: Drive + chunked-through-the-Worker, not R2/Supabase):** the browser slices the file (`File.slice`, never a whole-file read) into 16 MiB chunks (64 × Google's 256 KiB granule) → `PUT /api/uploads/<id>/chunk` → the Worker relays each chunk to the Drive resumable session it minted in `POST /api/uploads/start`. The capability session URI persists in new **`public.upload_sessions`** (`server/storage/db/upload_sessions.sql`, own-rows RLS, **migrated to production this session via MCP**) and is never returned to the browser. `GET …/status` probes Drive (`bytes */total`) for resume-from-offset; `POST …/complete` records the `drive_files` mapping (keeps the NEW-4 rollback: mapping-write failure deletes the Drive file + fails honestly — the V191 guard moved here). No single request is ever large → the Worker's ~100 MB body cap, its 128 MB memory, and Supabase's 50 MB cap all stop mattering, at any total size. Client loop (`src/shared/files/chunkedUpload.js`): sequential chunks, 5× exponential backoff, resume via /status after a drop, `storageQuotaExceeded` → plain-English "Drive is full" without futile retries; Library tray shows an honest per-file **progress bar** (server-confirmed bytes).
- **Download half (this is what "the big file won't open" was): `GET /api/files` now STREAMS** — the Drive body passes through as a ReadableStream (the old handler buffered `arrayBuffer()` in the Worker, blowing the 128 MB memory cap on a 125 MB PDF) — **and forwards the client's `Range` → 206 Partial Content** (`adapter.fetchStream` / `driveBackend.getStream` / `driveClient.mediaStream`). Drive-stored PDFs > 50 MB open BY URL (`driveStreamSource` + URL-source `loadPdf`), so pdf.js range-streams them progressively; the buffered path stays the fallback and for everything else.
- **Removed (per the handoff §9):** the whole-file `POST /api/files` route, `functions/api/files/resumable.js` (browser-direct), `reviewStore.uploadLargeToDrive` + `uploadSource`, and the **Supabase Storage upload fallback** in `storeSource` (the 50 MB fallback IS what produced the silent "oversize" dead end; Supabase Storage reads remain for pre-cutover files). ALL uploads — any size — now take the one chunked path; `sourceState`'s `oversize`/`too-large` states remain only to classify legacy never-stored records.
- **Post-review hardening (same session — a 5-lens adversarial review over the diff; 2 findings double-confirmed, 15 triaged):** the chunk endpoint no longer order-checks against its own best-effort bookkeeping (a missed progress write could 400 a healthy upload; Drive arbitrates offsets authoritatively); `/complete` is **idempotent** (the row is marked `recorded` and kept until expiry, so a retry after a lost response succeeds instead of 404ing a fully-successful upload — status CHECK extended via a second production migration) and a rolled-back session answers a distinct 410 + `sessionLost`; the client **short-circuits `sessionLost`** (no futile retry burn), **re-reads the auth token per request** via a getter (an upload outliving the ~1 h JWT no longer dies mid-flight), resets its retry budget when the /status probe shows progress (bodies landing while responses drop), validates the server's chunkSize granularity, and maps a quota failure at session-mint too; the **real failure cause** (e.g. "Google Drive is out of storage space") now reaches all three surfaces — the Library tray (`fileWarn`), the DocReview banner, and a NEW Stitcher store-failure banner (the Stitcher previously lost a failed store silently); split uploads share one continuous progress bar. **Known residuals (accepted, minor):** pdf.js range reads pin the open-time token, so a page first fetched >1 h after opening can 401 (re-open recovers); a tab closed in the seconds between the final chunk and `/complete` can orphan one Drive file (the 7-day purge removes only the row).
- Verify: live (concurrency/timing + real-project-data + range/parity — mandatory LIVE-VERIFY classes) → **V282**: signed-in ≥100 MB upload completes with a moving progress bar + lands in Drive; opens in the viewer with `206` responses in the network tab; killing the network mid-upload resumes (not restarts).
- Sandbox: full suite green (new `test/chunkedUpload.test.js` · `resumableProxy.test.js` · `uploadEndpoints.test.js` · `filesStream.test.js` — chunk math incl. final-short-chunk / exact-multiple / 256 KiB granularity, **308-as-success**, resume-from-offset, retry cap, quota short-circuit, foreign-uploadId → 404 before Drive is touched (B491), session-URI-never-in-a-response, init→308s→200 integration, Range→206 passthrough + the V150 two-account no-bytes regression) · lint 0 · build green + lazy chunks intact.
